page-Chinese_remainder_theorem rootpage-Chinese_remainder_theorem skin-vector action-view\">\n<div id=\"mw-page-base\" class=\"noprint\"></div>\n<div id=\"mw-head-base\" class=\"noprint\"></div>\n<div id=\"content\" class=\"mw-body\" role=\"main\">\n\t<a id=\"top\"></a>\n\t\t<div id=\"siteNotice\" class=\"mw-body-content\"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t<div class=\"mw-indicators mw-body-content\">\n</div>\n\n\t<h1 id=\"firstHeading\" class=\"firstHeading\" lang=\"en\">Chinese remainder theorem</h1>\n\t\n\t<div id=\"bodyContent\" class=\"mw-body-content\">\n\t\t<div id=\"siteSub\" class=\"noprint\">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id=\"contentSub\"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t\n\t\t<div id=\"jump-to-nav\"></div>\n\t\t<a class=\"mw-jump-link\" href=\"#mw-head\">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t<a class=\"mw-jump-link\" href=\"#p-search\">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t<div id=\"mw-content-text\" lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\" class=\"mw-content-ltr\"><div class=\"mw-parser-output\"><div class=\"shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux\" style=\"display:none\">Theorem for solving simultaneous congruences</div>\n<div class=\"thumb tright\"><div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width:222px;\"><a href=\"/wiki/File:Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"\" src=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg/220px-Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg.png\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"220\" height=\"330\" class=\"thumbimage\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg/330px-Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg/440px-Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg.png 2x\" data-file-width=\"512\" data-file-height=\"768\" /></a>  <div class=\"thumbcaption\"><div class=\"magnify\"><a href=\"/wiki/File:Sun_Tzu_Chinese_remainder_theorem.svg\" class=\"internal\" title=\"Enlarge\"></a></div>Sun-tzu's original formulation: <span class=\"nowrap\"><i>x</i> &#8801; 2 (mod 3)</span> <span class=\"nowrap\">&#8801; 3 (mod 5)</span> <span class=\"nowrap\">&#8801; 2 (mod 7)</span> <span class=\"nowrap\">with the solution</span> <span class=\"nowrap\"><i>x</i> = 23 + 105<i>k</i></span> <span class=\"nowrap\">where <i>k</i> &#8712; \u2124</span></div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href=\"/wiki/Number_theory\" title=\"Number theory\">number theory</a>, the <b>Chinese remainder theorem</b> states that if one knows the remainders of the <a href=\"/wiki/Euclidean_division\" title=\"Euclidean division\">Euclidean division</a> of an <a href=\"/wiki/Integer\" title=\"Integer\">integer</a> <i>n</i> by several integers, then one can determine uniquely the remainder of the division of <i>n</i> by the product of these integers, under the condition that the <a href=\"/wiki/Divisor\" title=\"Divisor\">divisors</a> are <a href=\"/wiki/Pairwise_coprime\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Pairwise coprime\">pairwise coprime</a>.\n</p><p>The earliest known statement of the theorem is by the Chinese mathematician Sun-tzu in the <i><a href=\"/wiki/Sunzi_Suanjing\" title=\"Sunzi Suanjing\">Sun-tzu Suan-ching</a></i> in the 3rd century AD.\n</p><p>The Chinese remainder theorem is widely used for computing with large integers, as it allows replacing a computation for which one knows a bound on the size of the result by several similar computations on small integers.\n</p><p>The Chinese remainder theorem (expressed in terms of <a href=\"/wiki/Modular_arithmetic#Congruence_relation\" title=\"Modular arithmetic\">congruences</a>) is true over every <a href=\"/wiki/Principal_ideal_domain\" title=\"Principal ideal domain\">principal ideal domain</a>. It has been generalized to any <a href=\"/wiki/Commutative_ring\" title=\"Commutative ring\">commutative ring</a>, with a formulation involving <a href=\"/wiki/Ideal_(ring_theory)\" title=\"Ideal (ring theory)\">ideals</a>.\n</p>\n<div id=\"toc\" class=\"toc\" role=\"navigation\" aria-labelledby=\"mw-toc-heading\"><input type=\"checkbox\" role=\"button\" id=\"toctogglecheckbox\" class=\"toctogglecheckbox\" style=\"display:none\" /><div class=\"toctitle\" lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><h2 id=\"mw-toc-heading\">Contents</h2><span class=\"toctogglespan\"><label class=\"toclevel-1 tocsection-27\"><a href=\"#See_also\"><span class=\"tocnumber\">10</span> <span class=\"toctext\">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class=\"toclevel-1 tocsection-28\"><a <span class=\"toctext\">References</span></a></li>\n<li class=\"toclevel-1 tocsection-30\"><a href=\"#Further_reading\"><span class=\"tocnumber\">13</span> <span class=\"toctext\">Further links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"History\">History</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: History\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The earliest known statement of the theorem, as a problem with specific numbers, appears in the 3rd-century book <i><a href=\"/wiki/Sunzi_Suanjing\" title=\"Sunzi Suanjing\"> Sun-tzu Suan-ching</a></i> by the Chinese mathematician Sun-tzu:<sup id=\"cite_ref-Katz_1-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-Katz-1\">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate=\"TemplateStyles:r886047036\">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class=\"templatequote\"><p>There are certain things whose number is unknown. If we count them by threes, we have two left over; by fives, we have three left over; and by sevens, two are left over. How many things are there?<sup id=\"cite_ref-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-2\">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Sun-tzu's work contains neither a proof nor a full algorithm.<sup id=\"cite_ref-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-3\">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> What amounts to an algorithm for solving this problem was described by <a href=\"/wiki/Aryabhata\" title=\"Aryabhata\">Aryabhata</a> (6th century).<sup id=\"cite_ref-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-4\">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Special cases of the Chinese remainder theorem were also known to <a href=\"/wiki/Brahmagupta\" title=\"Brahmagupta\">Brahmagupta</a> (7th century), and appear in <a href=\"/wiki/Fibonacci\" title=\"Fibonacci\">Fibonacci</a>'s <a href=\"/wiki/Liber_Abaci\" title=\"Liber Abaci\">Liber Abaci</a> (1202).<sup id=\"cite_ref-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-5\">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The result was later generalized with a complete solution called <i>Ta-yan-shu</i> (<span lang=\"zh\" title=\"Chinese language text\">\u5927\u884d\u8853</span>) in <a href=\"/wiki/Qin_Jiushao\" title=\"Qin Jiushao\">Ch'in Chiu-shao</a>'s 1247 <i><a href=\"/wiki/Mathematical_Treatise_in_Nine_Sections\" title=\"Mathematical Treatise in Nine Sections\">Mathematical Treatise in Nine Sections</a></i> (<span lang=\"zh\" title=\"Chinese language text\">\u6578\u66f8\u4e5d\u7ae0</span>, <i>Shu-shu Chiu-chang</i>)<sup id=\"cite_ref-6\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-6\">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> which was translated into English in early 19th century by British missionary <a href=\"/wiki/Alexander_Wylie_(missionary)\" title=\"Alexander Wylie (missionary)\">Alexander Wylie</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-7\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-7\">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class=\"thumb tright\"><div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width:222px;\"><a href=\"/wiki/File:Disqvisitiones-800.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"\" src=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Disqvisitiones-800.jpg/220px-Disqvisitiones-800.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"220\" height=\"368\" class=\"thumbimage\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Disqvisitiones-800.jpg/330px-Disqvisitiones-800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Disqvisitiones-800.jpg/440px-Disqvisitiones-800.jpg 2x\" data-file-width=\"478\" data-file-height=\"800\" /></a>  <div class=\"thumbcaption\"><div class=\"magnify\"><a href=\"/wiki/File:Disqvisitiones-800.jpg\" class=\"internal\" title=\"Enlarge\"></a></div>The Chinese remainder theorem appears in <a href=\"/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss\" title=\"Carl Friedrich Gauss\">Gauss</a>'s 1801 book <i><a href=\"/wiki/Disquisitiones_Arithmeticae\" title=\"Disquisitiones Arithmeticae\">Disquisitiones Arithmeticae</a></i>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Gauss1801.loc=32-36_8-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-Gauss1801.loc=32-36-8\">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The notion of congruences was first introduced and used by <a href=\"/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss\" title=\"Carl Friedrich Gauss\">Gauss</a> in his <i>Disquisitiones Arithmeticae</i> of 1801.<sup id=\"cite_ref-9\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-9\">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Gauss illustrates the Chinese remainder theorem on a problem involving calendars, namely, \"to find the years that have a certain period number with respect to the solar and lunar cycle and the Roman indiction.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-10\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-10\">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Gauss introduces a procedure for solving the problem that had already been used by <a href=\"/wiki/Leonhard_Euler\" title=\"Leonhard Euler\">Euler</a> but was in fact an ancient method that had appeared several times.<sup id=\"cite_ref-11\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-11\">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Theorem_statement\">Theorem statement</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Theorem statement\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Let <i>n</i><sub>1</sub>, ..., <i>n</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> be integers greater than 1, which are often called <i><a href=\"/wiki/Modular_arithmetic\" title=\"Modular arithmetic\">moduli</a></i> or <i><a href=\"/wiki/Euclidean_division\" title=\"Euclidean division\">divisors</a></i>. Let us denote by <i>N</i> the product of the <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>.\n</p><p>The Chinese remainder theorem asserts that if the <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> are <a href=\"/wiki/Pairwise_coprime\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Pairwise coprime\">pairwise coprime</a>, and if <i>a</i><sub>1</sub>, ..., <i>a</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> are integers such that 0 \u2264 <i>a</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> &lt; <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> for every <i>i</i>, then there is one and only one integer <i>x</i>, such that 0 \u2264 <i>x</i> &lt; <i>N</i> and the remainder of the <a href=\"/wiki/Euclidean_division\" title=\"Euclidean division\">Euclidean division</a> of <i>x</i> by <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> is <i>a</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> for every <i>i</i>.\n</p><p>This may be restated as follows in term of <a href=\"/wiki/Congruence_relation\" title=\"Congruence relation\">congruences</a>:\nIf the <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> are pairwise coprime, and if <i>a</i><sub>1</sub>, ..., <i>a</i><sub><i>k</i></sub> are any integers, then there exist integers <i>x</i> such that\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}x&amp;\\equiv a_{1}{\\pmod {n_{1}}}\\\\&amp;\\,\\,\\,\\vdots \\\\x&amp;\\equiv a_{k}{\\pmod {n_{k}}},\\end{aligned}}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n {n_{k}}},\\end{aligned}}}\"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>and any two solutions, say <i>x</i><sub>1</sub> and <i>x</i><sub>2</sub>, are congruent modulo <i>N</i>, that is, <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>x</i><sub>1</sub> \u2261 <i>x</i><sub>2</sub> (mod <i>N</i>)</span>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-12\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-12\">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href=\"/wiki/Abstract_algebra\" title=\"Abstract algebra\">abstract algebra</a>, the theorem is often restated as: if the <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub> are pairwise coprime, the map\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span {n}}_{k})}\"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>defines a <a href=\"/wiki/Ring_isomorphism\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Ring isomorphism\">ring isomorphism</a><sup id=\"cite_ref-13\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-13\">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /N\\mathbb {Z} \\cong \\mathbb {Z} /n_{1}\\mathbb {Z} \\times \\cdots \\times \\mathbb {Z} /n_{k}\\mathbb {Z} }\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi        <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>&#x2245;<!-- \u2245 --></mo>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow       <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- \u00d7 --></mo>\n        <mo>&#x22EF;<!-- \u22ef --></mo>\n        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- \u00d7 --></mo>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /N\\mathbb {Z} \\cong \\mathbb {Z} /n_{1}\\mathbb {Z} \\times \\cdots \\times \\mathbb {Z} /n_{k}\\mathbb {Z} }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5809e369d284254f4e2945283cf30cce5d2b881\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:31.288ex; height:2.843ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /N\\mathbb {Z} \\cong \\mathbb {Z} /n_{1}\\mathbb {Z} \\times \\cdots \\times \\mathbb {Z} /n_{k}\\mathbb {Z} }\"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>between the <a href=\"/wiki/Ring_(mathematics)\" title=\"Ring (mathematics)\">ring</a> of <a href=\"/wiki/Integers_modulo_n\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Integers modulo n\">integers modulo <i>N</i></a> and the <a href=\"/wiki/Direct_product\" title=\"Direct product\">direct product</a> of the rings of integers modulo the <i>n</i><sub><i>i</i></sub>. This means that for doing a sequence of arithmetic operations in <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /N\\mathbb {Z} ,}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>N</mi>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /N\\mathbb {Z} ,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/341b93009d0a623d7b5df95b80ad8133fdbae32b\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.974ex; height:2.843ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /N\\mathbb {Z} ,}\"/></span> one may do the same computation independently in each <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /n_{i}\\mathbb {Z} }\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mi mathvariant=\"double-struck\">Z</mi>\n        </mrow>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /n_{i}\\mathbb {Z} }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5586f1c5f0918244458c886a5ec88a517096a589\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.458ex; height:2.843ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle \\mathbb {Z} /n_{i}\\mathbb {Z} }\"/></span> and then get the result by applying the isomorphism (from the right to the left). This may be much faster than the direct computation if <i>N</i> and the number of operations are large. This is widely used, under the name <i>multi-modular computation</i>, for <a href=\"/wiki/Linear_algebra\" title=\"Linear algebra\">linear algebra</a> over the integers or the <a href=\"/wiki/Rational_number\" title=\"Rational number\">rational numbers</a>.\n</p><p>The theorem can also be restated in the language of <a href=\"/wiki/Combinatorics\" title=\"Combinatorics\">combinatorics</a> as the fact that the infinite <a href=\"/wiki/Arithmetic_progression\" title=\"Arithmetic progression\">arithmetic progressions</a> of integers form a <a href=\"/wiki/Helly_family\" title=\"Helly family\">Helly family</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-14\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-14\">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Proof\">Proof</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Proof\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The existence and the uniqueness of the solution may be proven independently. However, the first proof of existence, given below, uses this uniqueness.\n</p>\n<h3><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Uniqueness\">Uniqueness</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Uniqueness\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Suppose that <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">x</span> and <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">y</span> are both solutions to all the congruences. As <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">x</span> and <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">y</span> give the same remainder, when divided by <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>n<sub>i</sub></i></span>, their difference <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>x</i> \u2212 <i>y</i></span> is a multiple of each <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>n<sub>i</sub></i></span>. As the <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>n<sub>i</sub></i></span> are pairwise coprime, their product <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>N</i></span> divides also <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>x</i> \u2212 <i>y</i></span>, and thus <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">x</span> and <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">y</span> are congruent modulo <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>N</i></span>. If <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">x</span> and <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">y</span>  are supposed to be non negative and less than <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>N</i></span> (as in the first statement of the theorem), then their difference may be a multiple of <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>N</i></span> only if <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>x</i> = <i>y</i></span>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id=\"Existence_.28first_proof.29\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Existence_(first_proof)\">Existence (first proof)</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Existence (first proof)\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The map\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle x{\\bmod {N}}\\mapsto (x{\\bmod {n}}_{1},\\ldots ,x{\\bmod {n}}_{k})}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mi>x</mi>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mo lspace=\"thickmathspace\" rspace=\"thickmathspace\">mod</mo>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>N</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo stretchy=\"false\">&#x21A6;<!-- \u21a6 --></mo>\n        <mo stretchy=\"false\">(</mo>\n        <mi>x</mi>\n        <msub>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mo lspace=\"thickmathspace\" rspace=\"thickmathspace\">mod</mo>\n            <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n              <mi>n</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n        <mo>&#x2026;<!-- \u2026 --></mo>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n        <mi>x</mi>\n        <msub>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mo lspace=\"thickmathspace\" rspace=\"thickmathspace\">mod</mo>\n            <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n              <mi>n</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>k</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo stretchy=\"false\">)</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle x{\\bmod {N}}\\mapsto (x{\\bmod {n}}_{1},\\ldots ,x{\\bmod {n}}_{k})}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1fa122f7e6c5927f8a27f0e47b4a7b510ce22033\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:38.63ex; height:2.843ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle x{\\bmod {N}}\\mapsto (x{\\bmod {n}}_{1},\\ldots ,x{\\bmod {n}}_{k})}\"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>maps congruence classes modulo <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>N</i></span> to sequences of congruence classes modulo <span class=\"texhtml\"><i>n<sub>i</sub></i></span>. The proof of uniqueness shows that this map is <a href=\"/wiki/Injective\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Injective\">injective</a>. As the <a href=\"/wiki/Domain_of_a_function\" title=\"Domain of a function\">domain</a> and the <a href=\"/wiki/Codomain\" title=\"Codomain\">codomain</a> of this map have the same number of elements, the map is also <a href=\"/wiki/Surjective\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Surjective\">surjective</a>, which proves the existence of the solution.\n</p><p>This proof is very simple but does not provide any direct way for computing a solution. Moreover, it cannot be generalized to other situations where the following proof can.\n</p>\n<h3><span id=\"Existence_.28constructive_proof.29\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Existence_(constructive_proof)\">Existence (constructive proof)</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Existence (constructive proof)\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Existence may be established by an explicit construction of <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">x</span>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-15\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"#cite_note-15\">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> This construction may be split into two steps, firstly by solving the problem in the case of two moduli, and the second one by extending this solution to the general case by <a href=\"/wiki/Mathematical_induction\" title=\"Mathematical induction\">induction</a> on the number of moduli.\n</p>\n<h4><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Case_of_two_moduli\">Case of two moduli</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Case of two moduli\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>We want to solve the system:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" {n_{2}}},\\end{aligned}}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mtable <mtr>\n              <mtd>\n                <mi>x</mi>\n              </mtd>\n              <mtd>\n                <mi></mi>\n                <mo>&#x2261;<!-- \u2261 --></mo>\n                <msub>\n                  <mi>a</mi>\n                  <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n                    <mn>1</mn>\n                  </mrow>\n                </msub>\n                <mrow />\n                  <msub>\n                    <mi>n</mi>\n                    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n                      <mn>1</mn>\n                    </mrow>\n       </mtd>\n              <mtd>\n                <mi></mi>\n                <mo>&#x2261;<!-- \u2261 --></mo>\n                <msub>\n                  <mi>a</mi>\n                  <mrow <mi>n</mi>\n                    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n                      <mn>2</mn>\n                    </mrow>\n                  </msub>\n                  <mo <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}x&amp;\\equiv a_{1}{\\pmod {n_{1}}}\\\\x&amp;\\equiv a_{2}{\\pmod {n_{2}}},\\end{aligned}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09c78dea4f052c5be46a5efbc3b23447e0dabc70\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" {n_{k}}},\\end{aligned}}}\"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where the <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math width:2.194ex; height:2.009ex;\" alt=\"n_{i}\"/></span> are pairwise coprime. The two first equations have a solution <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle a_{1,2}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>a</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n            <mo>,</mo>\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle a_{1,2}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b5af437e48bc8be86dca7ffc1009dcba3bdaee18\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.563ex; height:2.343ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle a_{1,2}}\"/></span> provided by the method of the previous section. The set of the solutions of these two first equations is the set of all solutions of the equation\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle x\\equiv a_{1,2}{\\pmod {n_{1}n_{2}}}.}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mi>x</mi>\n        <mo>&#x2261;<!-- \u2261 --></mo>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>a</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n            <mo>,</mo>\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mspace width=\"1em\" />\n          <mo stretchy=\"false\">(</mo>\n          <mi>mod</mi>\n          <mspace width=\"0.333em\" />\n          <msub>\n            <mi>n</mi>\n            <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n              <mn>1</mn>\n            </mrow>\n          </msub>\n          <msub>\n            <mi>n</mi>\n            <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n              <mn>2</mn>\n            </mrow>\n          </msub>\n          <mo stretchy=\"false\">)</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle x\\equiv a_{1,2}{\\pmod {n_{1}n_{2}}}.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8239c71a2b9e8f49c7a7564291f66eaea57f6b38\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:23.22ex; height:3.009ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle x\\equiv a_{1,2}{\\pmod {n_{1}n_{2}}}.}\"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>As the other <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle n_{i}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle n_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/57f87f905ba5a4d8c691ccaecd65fc47bd007ba4\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.194ex; height:2.009ex;\" alt=\"n_{i}\"/></span> are coprime with <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle n_{1}n_{2},}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mn>1</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle n_{1}n_{2},}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a2deeaa891bfe0706d9c97bf82d4d44606523aa6\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.545ex; height:2.009ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle n_{1}n_{2},}\"/></span> this reduces solving the initial problem of <span class=\"texhtml mvar\" style=\"font-style:italic;\">k</span> equations to a similar problem with <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle k-1}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mi>k</mi>\n        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- \u2212 --></mo>\n        <mn>1</mn>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle k-1}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/21363ebd7038c93aae93127e7d910fc1b2e2c745\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:5.214ex; height:2.343ex;\" alt=\"k-1\"/></span> equations. Iterating the process, one gets eventually the solutions of the initial problem.\n</p>\n<h3><span id=\"Existence_.28direct_construction.29\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Existence_(direct_construction)\">Existence (direct construction)</span><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a href=\"/w/index.php?title=Chinese_remainder_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Existence (direct construction)\">edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For constructing a solution, it is not necessary to make an induction on the number of moduli. However, such a direct construction involves more computation with large numbers, which makes it less efficient and less used. Nevertheless, <a href=\"/wiki/Lagrange_interpolation\" class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Lagrange interpolation\">Lagrange interpolation</a> is a special case of this construction, applied to polynomials instead of integers.\n</p><p>Let <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle N_{i}=N/n_{i}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>N</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>N</mi>\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle N_{i}=N/n_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b2ba3f3afcf7097176ce5442a175d0760f12d4d8\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.185ex; height:2.843ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle N_{i}=N/n_{i}}\"/></span> be the product of all moduli but one. As the <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle n_{i}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle n_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/57f87f905ba5a4d8c691ccaecd65fc47bd007ba4\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.194ex; height:2.009ex;\" alt=\"n_{i}\"/></span> are pairwise coprime, <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle N_{i}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>N</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle N_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fef58cebf23adff9199f17325aefb5515fdca99d\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.666ex; height:2.509ex;\" alt=\"N_{i}\"/></span> and <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle n_{i}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>n</mi>\n          <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n            <mi>i</mi>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle n_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/57f87f905ba5a4d8c691ccaecd65fc47bd007ba4\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.194ex; height:2.009ex;\" alt=\"n_{i}\"/></span> are coprime. Thus <a href=\"/wiki/B%C3%A9zout%27s_identity\" title=\"B\u00e9zout&#39;s identity\">B\u00e9zout's identity</a> applies, and there exist integers <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle M_{i}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img width:3.054ex; height:2.509ex;\" alt=\"M_{i}\"/></span> and <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math    </msub>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle N=n_{1}n_{2}\\cdots n_{k}.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/28edd06ff4296e5d8ee47063e7d638ea89edd0a8\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" solution for <span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\" <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle x}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle 0\\leq x&lt;N,}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" <annotation encoding=\"application/x-tex\">{\\displaystyle 0\\leq x&lt;N,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src=\"https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e33526a59c19462338c42fd6cb7d6301dbb10d9\" class=\"mwe-math-fallback-image-inline\" aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.4ex; height:2.509ex;\" alt=\"{\\displaystyle 0\\leq x&lt;N,}\"/></span> and these methods are applied on the example:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class=\"mwe-math-element\"><span class=\"mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y\" style=\"display: none;\"><math xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML\"  alttext=\"{\\displaystyle {\\begin{aligned}x&amp;\\equiv 0{\\pmod {3}}\\\\x&amp;\\equiv 3{\\pmod {4}}\\\\x&amp;\\equiv 4{\\pmod {5}}.\\end{aligned}}}\">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n      <mstyle displaystyle=\"true\" scriptlevel=\"0\">\n        <mrow class=\"MJX-TeXAtom-ORD\">\n          <mtable columnalign=\"right left right left right left right left right left right left\" rowspacing=\"3pt\" columnspacing=\"0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em
